    2318             : 
    2319             : /* Return the anti-affinity score, which is a measure of the amount of
    2320             :  * violations of anti-affinity in the current cluster layout, that is, how
    2321             :  * badly the masters and slaves are distributed in the different IP
    2322             :  * addresses so that slaves of the same master are not in the master
    2323             :  * host and are also in different hosts.
    2324             :  *
    2325             :  * The score is calculated as follows:
    2326             :  *
    2327             :  * SAME_AS_MASTER = 10000 * each slave in the same IP of its master.
    2328             :  * SAME_AS_SLAVE  = 1 * each slave having the same IP as another slave
    2329             :                       of the same master.
    2330             :  * FINAL_SCORE = SAME_AS_MASTER + SAME_AS_SLAVE
    2331             :  *
    2332             :  * So a greater score means a worse anti-affinity level, while zero
    2333             :  * means perfect anti-affinity.
    2334             :  *
    2335             :  * The anti affinity optimizator will try to get a score as low as
    2336             :  * possible. Since we do not want to sacrifice the fact that slaves should
    2337             :  * not be in the same host as the master, we assign 10000 times the score
    2338             :  * to this violation, so that we'll optimize for the second factor only
    2339             :  * if it does not impact the first one.
    2340             :  *
    2341             :  * The ipnodes argument is an array of clusterManagerNodeArray, one for
    2342             :  * each IP, while ip_count is the total number of IPs in the configuration.
    2343             :  *
    2344             :  * The function returns the above score, and the list of
    2345             :  * offending slaves can be stored into the 'offending' argument,
    2346             :  * so that the optimizer can try changing the configuration of the
    2347             :  * slaves violating the anti-affinity goals. */
    2348           0 : static int clusterManagerGetAntiAffinityScore(clusterManagerNodeArray *ipnodes,
    2349             :     int ip_count, clusterManagerNode ***offending, int *offending_len)
    2350             : {
    2351           0 :     int score = 0, i, j;
    2352           0 :     int node_len = cluster_manager.nodes->len;
    2353           0 :     clusterManagerNode **offending_p = NULL;
    2354           0 :     if (offending != NULL) {
    2355           0 :         *offending = zcalloc(node_len * sizeof(clusterManagerNode*));
    2356           0 :         offending_p = *offending;
    2357             :     }
    2358             :     /* For each set of nodes in the same host, split by
    2359             :      * related nodes (masters and slaves which are involved in
    2360             :      * replication of each other) */
    2361           0 :     for (i = 0; i < ip_count; i++) {
    2362           0 :         clusterManagerNodeArray *node_array = &(ipnodes[i]);
    2363           0 :         dict *related = dictCreate(&clusterManagerDictType, NULL);
    2364           0 :         char *ip = NULL;
    2365           0 :         for (j = 0; j < node_array->len; j++) {

    2544             : /* -----------------------------------------------------------------------------
    2545             :  * Key space handling

    2547             : 
    2548             : /* We have 16384 hash slots. The hash slot of a given key is obtained
    2549             :  * as the least significant 14 bits of the crc16 of the key.
    2550             :  *
    2551             :  * However if the key contains the {...} pattern, only the part between
    2552             :  * { and } is hashed. This may be useful in the future to force certain
    2553             :  * keys to be in the same node (assuming no resharding is in progress). */
    2554           0 : static unsigned int clusterManagerKeyHashSlot(char *key, int keylen) {
    2555           0 :     int s, e; /* start-end indexes of { and } */
    2556             : 
    2557           0 :     for (s = 0; s < keylen; s++)
    2558           0 :         if (key[s] == '{') break;
    2559             : 
    2560             :     /* No '{' ? Hash the whole key. This is the base case. */
    2561           0 :     if (s == keylen) return crc16(key,keylen) & 0x3FFF;
    2562             : 
    2563             :     /* '{' found? Check if we have the corresponding '}'. */
    2564           0 :     for (e = s+1; e < keylen; e++)
    2565           0 :         if (key[e] == '}') break;
    2566             : 
    2567             :     /* No '}' or nothing between {} ? Hash the whole key. */
    2568           0 :     if (e == keylen || e == s+1) return crc16(key,keylen) & 0x3FFF;
    2569             : 
    2570             :     /* If we are here there is both a { and a } on its right. Hash
    2571             :      * what is in the middle between { and }. */
    2572           0 :     return crc16(key+s+1,e-s-1) & 0x3FFF;
    2573             : }
